Part IV
Report of the Military Staff Committee
I. Introduction
1.
The present report of the Military Staff Committee covers the period from
1 January to 31 December 2017.

II. Background
2.
The Military Staff Committee was established pursuant to Article 47 of the
Charter of the United Nations and Security Council resolution 1 (1946). The
Committee has a mandate to advise and assist the Security Council on all questions
relating to the Council’s military requirements for the maintenance of international
peace and security, the employment and command of forces placed at its disposal, the
regulation of armaments, and possible disarmament.

III. Summary of the activities of the Committee
3.
The Committee functioned continuously under its revised draft statue and revised
draft rules of procedure, contained in document S/115 of 1 August 1946, during the
period under review. The Committee held a total of 30 meetings and discussed a total
of 37 topics (55 agenda items). During the reporting period, the Committee conducted
two field missions to current United Nations peacekeeping operations.
4.
Military representatives of the elected members of the Security Council
participated in 25 meetings. Representatives of Secretariat departments participated in
discussions: the Department of Peacekeeping Operations on 21 topics, the Department
of Political Affairs on 4 topics and the Department of Field Support on 1 topic.
5.
Current United Nations peacekeeping and special political missions were the
focus of 23 meetings:
(a)

African Union Mission in Somalia: one meeting;

(b)

United Nations Mission for the Referendum in Western Sahara: one meeting;

(c) United Nations Multidimensional Integrated Stabilization Mission in the
Central African Republic: one meeting;
(d) United Nations Multidimensional Integrated Stabilization Mission in
Mali: one meeting;
(e)

United Nations Stabilization Mission in Haiti: two meetings;

(f) United Nations Organization Stabilization Mission in the Democratic
Republic of the Congo: one meeting;

198/234

(g)

United Nations Assistance Mission in Afghanistan: one meeting;

(h)

United Nations Assistance Mission for Iraq: one meeting;

(i)

African Union-United Nations Hybrid Operation in Darfur: one meeting;

(j)

United Nations Disengagement Observer Force (UNDOF): two meetings;

(k)

United Nations Peacekeeping Force in Cyprus (UNFICYP): two meetings;

(l)

United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon (UNIFIL): one meeting;
18-14247

-----------------------Page 200 End-----------------------

Report of the Military Staff Committee

(m) United Nations Interim Security Force for Abyei: two meetings;

6.

(n)

United Nations Mission in South Sudan (UNMISS): one meeting;

(o)

United Nations Military Observer Group in India and Pakistan: one meeting;

(p)

United Nations Operation in Côte d’Ivoire: one meeting;

(q)

United Nations Support Mission in Libya: one meeting;

(r)

United Nations Assistance Mission in Somalia: one meeting;

(s)

United Nations Truce Supervision Organization (UNTSO): one meeting.

Eleven meetings included various thematic debates:
(a)

Challenges in the planning of peacekeeping operations;

(b)

Command and control in peacekeeping operations;

(c) Communication of United Nations peacekeeping operations with the
civilian population;
(d)

Improvised explosive device defeat within peacekeeping operations;

(e) Intelligence in the context of peacekeeping operations: assessment
capabilities in the Department of Peacekeeping Oper ations;
(f)

Military components in modern peacekeeping operations;

(g)

Partnership with the European Union Military Staff;

(h)

Predeployment training: striving for uniformity;

(i)

Protection of civilians in armed conflict;

(j)

Strategic force generation;

(k)

United Nations peacekeeping operations budget.

7.
The Committee conducted two missions to areas of current United Nations
peacekeeping operations.
8.
During the first mission, the Committee visited South Sudan from 1 to 5 March.
The primary purpose of the visit was to gain an in-depth understanding of UNMISS
and its capabilities.
9.
During the second mission, the Committee visited the Mediterranean, with stops
in Israel, Cyprus, Lebanon and Italy, from 14 to 22 November. The primary objectiv es
of the mission were to gain an in-depth understanding of UNTSO, UNDOF,
UNFICYP, UNIFIL and the Global Service Centre in Brindisi, Italy, and to assess
the military challenges and opportunities for those missions in executing mandates,
the appropriate allocation of resources and infrastructure, plans for the future of the
missions and conditions that might prompt a change in the structure of the forces.
10. The Committee continued to announce all meetings and provisional agendas in
the Journal of the United Nations and on its website (www.un.org/sc/suborg/en/
subsidiary/msc), which is available in the six official languages of the United Nations
and offers swift and easy access to the programme of work and current information
on the Committee.
11. In accordance with paragraph 178 of General Assembly resolution 60/1 entitled
“2005 World Summit Outcome”, the Committee continued to consider its
composition, mandate and working methods.
12. The Committee remained prepared to carry out the functions assigned to it under
the terms of Article 47 of the Charter.
